Appendix C
Generic Railway
Specication
This is the generic specication of the model. The le shown in section C.8
contains safety properties and this can be used for global model checking. How-
ever if one wish to do bounded model checking using induction, then the le
described in section C.9 should be used, as the invariants has been strengthened
for this le.

C.9 Including Strong Invariants
157
C.9
Including Strong Invariants
This is the ModelStronginvariants.rsl le for the generic specication of the rail-
way system, where the strengthened properties are included as one conjuncted
assertion. This should be used for bounded model checking with induction.

/\ req ( r , p) = T.MINUS /\
(( has_dir_down ( r ) /\
has_stem_down(p) ) \/ ( has_dir_up ( r ) /\ has_stem_up(p) )
) ) => vacant1 (MinusToStem [ p ] ) )
/\
−−[ground_unused_boundary_linear ]
RailwaySystem |−G
( a l l
l : T. LinearSectionId :−
is_boundary_sec ( l ) => vacant2 (UpToDown[ l ] ,DownToUp[ l ] ) )
/\
−−[points_vacant_in_lin_dir ]
RailwaySystem |−G
( a l l
p : T. PointId :−vacant2 (DownToUp[ p ] ,UpToDown[ p ] ) )
/\
−−[linears_vacant_in_point_dir ]
RailwaySystem |−G
( a l l
l : T. LinearSectionId :−vacant3 (StemToPM[ l ] ,

D.1.2
Generated.rsl
Here the Generated.rsl le for the Toy example is shown. The values all_linears,
all_points, all_sigs, all_routes, network, routetable and interlocking are used
by the Static.rsl le to extract information for the concrete system. Furthermore
in the bottom of the le a bunch of auxiliary values are dened that is also used
by the Static.rsl le.
The variables such as b12, mb11 and r3 for describing the sections, marker
boards and routes are not used directly referenced in the specication. The
sections, marker boards and routes are referenced by using their id and fetching
them from the all_linears, all_points, all_sigs and all_routes maps.

==PAGE:299==
Appendix G
Mail from SAL - Array
Index Problem
On 01/30/2015 10:43 AM, Jacob Bøgelund Hansen wrote:
G.1
Original Mail
Hi,
I have a speciation in SAL. See attached Test5.tar.gz. The main le id Test.sal.
The sal-wfc command terminates correctly with "OK". Running sal-smc, I get
the error message that the argument is not in the domain of the array. This
happens at the expression (line 32-35) at line 33:
IF s = 1 THEN ar[s] ELSE FALSE ENDIF
I would expect the sal-smc command to terminate tell me that the theorems
test, test2 and test4 are valid while the assertion test3 is invalid, but instead
I get the error message as in the attached screen-shot. This is weird as the
domain of ar is exactly 1.
==PAGE:300==
284
Mail from SAL - Array Index Problem
If I change line 33 of Test.sal so the above expression instead is:
IF s = 1 THEN ar[1] ELSE FALSE ENDIF
then it terminates correctly giving me a counter example for the theorem test3
and telling me that test, test2 and test4 are valid.
I nd this very odd, as ar[s] is inside an if-expression checking that s=1, so ar[s]
should only be evaluated for s=1. However somehow it seems that ar[s] is also
evaluated for s!=1.
Can someone tell me why the upper expressions give an error message, while
the lower one terminates correctly?
Best Regards Jacob Bøgelund Hansen Student at Technical University of Den-
mark
G.2
Reply
The problem is that SAL does not know that array ar has a nite domain (not
that the argument is not in the domain).
SAL does not "evaluate" the expression ar[s].
It tries to convert it into an
equivalent expression that can be processed by the bounded model checker.
This requires the domain of the array to be nite. Because your type has a
complicated denition, SAL can't gure out that it is nite. Your denition is
of the form
T : TYPE = i: int | P(i)
for some predicate P. SAL can't determine that only nitely many integers
satisfy the predicate P, so it can't say that T is nite.
The IF s=1 THEN ar[s] ... doesn't help, because SAL processes ar[s] indepen-
dently (without performing the substitution s := 1).
There's no problem with ar[1].
SAL can process this expression even if the
domain of the array is innite.
Bruno
